## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (population dynamics / bio-population growth ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt with features (t, P) indicates an ordinary differential equation for population size over time. Classical ecological models relate growth rate to current population P (density dependence), sometimes with explicit time forcing t (seasonality, harvesting, environmental change).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Constant immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (baseline input plus proportional growth/decline)
- Logistic growth (Verhulst) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) (choose c1 < 0 to represent carrying-capacity limitation)
- Generalized logistic (theta-logistic) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (flexible density dependence via exponent c2)
- Allee effect (strong/weak) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 + c2 * P) (positive density dependence at low P, limitation at high P)
- Gompertz-type growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (decelerating growth where per-capita rate declines with log(P))
- Ricker-type continuous approximation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * P)) (overcompensatory density dependence when c2 < 0, c1 < 0)
- Harvesting/removal (linear): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (constant quota when c1 < 0; net growth otherwise)
- Harvesting/removal (proportional + quota): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 + c2 * P (separable natural growth and proportional harvest terms)
- Saturating harvest (Holling-II style): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P / (P + c2) (catch/harvest saturates at high P)
- Time-varying intrinsic rate (seasonal): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic forcing on per-capita growth)
- Time-varying carrying capacity proxy: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (environmental fluctuations added to growth rate)
- Piecewise/threshold regulation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * Max(P - c2, 0)) (extra density dependence beyond a threshold)
- Environmental trend forcing: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (gradually changing per-capita growth due to long-term drivers)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-independent growth → dP_dt proportional to P (straight-line on log(P) vs t; per-capita rate constant).
- Carrying capacity / crowding → negative curvature in dP_dt vs P, often implemented via a negative P^2 term (e.g., P*(1 + c*P) with c < 0).
- Overcompensation (boom-bust tendency) → exponential-in-P modulation of per-capita growth, e.g., P*exp(c*P) with c < 0 producing rapid slowdown at high P.
- Allee effects (difficulty at low density) → factors like (c*P - 1) multiplying P, creating dP_dt < 0 at small P and positive growth above a threshold.
- Gompertz-like regulation → log(c*P) term gives per-capita growth decreasing approximately linearly with log(P).
- Harvesting/removal → subtractive terms independent of P (quota) or proportional to P (effort-based), shifting the dP_dt curve downward and potentially creating extinction equilibria.
- Saturating harvest/predation pressure → rational term P/(P+c) yields near-linear removal at low P and capped removal at high P.
- Seasonality → sin(c*t + phase) or cos(c*t + phase) multiplying P produces periodic oscillations in per-capita growth rate.
- Long-term environmental change → (c0 + c1*t) prefactor on P captures gradual drift in intrinsic growth (e.g., climate trend).
- Regime shifts / density thresholds → Max(P-c,0) or piecewise terms represent abrupt changes in regulation once P crosses a critical level.

GT: -c0*c1*P + c2*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P**c6 + c7*P
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (with fixed constants) is a function of **P only**:
\[
f(P)=A\,P + B\,P^2 + C\,P^{1/3}
\]
because
\[
-6.2168\cdot 1.41275\,P + 0.85788(1-P/79.2026)P +0.85788P^{1/3}+0.85788P
\]
expands to
- linear term: \(\big(-6.2168\cdot1.41275 +0.85788+0.85788\big)P\)
- quadratic term: \(-0.85788/79.2026\; P^2\) (nonzero)
- fractional-power term: \(0.85788\,P^{1/3}\) (nonzero)
- **no constant term, no logs/exp/sin/sqrt, no t-dependence, no rational-in-P denominators, no shifted \((P+c)^{1/3}\)**.

So any matching candidate must be reducible (by choosing its free constants) to exactly \(aP+bP^2+cP^{1/3}\) with \(b\neq 0\) and \(c\neq 0\), and with no extra terms.

### 1

This matches for all P. **Yes.**
